<rate>5< /rate>< Text>
My wife and I look for a Swiss restaurant in every city we visit, with nothing but disappointment (or mediocrity) to be found... until this one. This took us right back to Switzerland! The interior is both beautiful and spotlessly clean, the service was flawless, and the food was amazing! The menu here is very small but very authentic, and the restaurant is better for it. We shared one serving of raclette for appetizer and then shared a two-person serving of Emmental fondue, and left feeling almost disgustingly full. A wonderful place, and one we'll certainly return to next time we're in SF!< /Text>

107853167847068248186</UserId.>
< username>
Nicolas Noble< /username>
<date>1578807972800<//date><rate>2< /rate><Text>I pondered a while before making this review, but a few people asked me to post it, so here goes.

We're a group of French friends who used to come to the previous version of this restaurant, until it closed a few months ago, and reopened with new owners.

The change isn't for the better.

The gist of it is it seems the new owners don't seem to understand how to run a fondue restaurant.

Various issues we've had with the new version:
- The wine selection was fairly poor.
- There is no more salad automatically served with your fondue. That's sort of a small gotcha, but eating cheese fondue without an acidic salad at the beginning is going to do a number on your digestion.
- The only starter salad is way too sweet.
- There is only two cheese fondues on the menu. The previous restaurant had a lot more options.
- The two cheese fondues are virtually the same in taste, and are fairly bland.
- The bread comes in thick slices. That's the biggest issue we had while eating there. Who does that, seriously? Bread when used in a fondue is supposed to be diced. We spent a lot of frustrating time cutting our bread into smaller chunks. That was for us the biggest clue that whomever is running this restaurant now doesn't know what's involved in eating fondue.
- The vegetables served are pickled onions, garlic and peppers. That's disgusting. You'd usually want button mushrooms, diced granny smith apples, carrots, broccoli, and nothing pickled.
- The baby potatoes were in fact undercooked fingerling red potatoes. You usually want something smoother, such as rattes. And better cooked.
- The chocolate fondue... was a disaster. Extremely sweet, with way too much s'mores inside the pot, and no fruits. They serve speculoos cookies and other extremely sweet cookies, and no fruits. Who does this? The chocolate fondue needs to be much darker, less sweet, and served with fruits like pineapples, apples, grapes, strawberries, and maybe a few cookies of marshmallows, but these should be more rare.

All in all, we might give this restaurant another go in a year or so in case anything evolved, since we went there fairly soon after it reopened, and there might have been growing pains, but we will most likely avoid it from now on.</Text><pictures>None<//pictures>< response>
None</response>

< review>
This is a unique place. Most importantly, the food is remarkable. Best fondue in the city. I can't get enough of the oh la la. Go for a cheese and an oil. Get the apples and kiwis and meats and pineapples and everything. Don't be afraid to experiment with the flavors.

There is a true mountain getaway ambiance to the restaurant. You'd never know it from the small sign hanging the alcove of the commerical building on Van Ness, but the interior is clad in wood. The booths have intricate carvings.

Sadly, the glory that is the Matterhorn will cease to exist sometime this year. The owners are hanging it up. Get in there when you can so you don't miss out on this San Francisco hidden gem.<//review>

<Review>I love indoor cycling because it is the perfect combination of endurance, strength, cardio, and interval training.I have been to numerous cycling studios, some franchises like Flywheel itself and other more unique, smaller businesses. I have  also seen a good range of studio quality, varying from dirty bathrooms (I feel uncomfortable using their showers) to free towel and toiletries topped with an after class brunch.  I have also experienced challenging workouts that I thought was worth my time to workouts that I needed to modify constantly to make it count.

I visited Flywheel when I was visiting SF a month ago and it was the best cycling franchise I have been to. The instructor was helpful, upbeat, and most importantly the class consisted of different movements on the bike that challenged different muscle groups, all to the tune of good music. Like other franchises, they have a TV screen showing the top cyclists in class but it only popped up a few times in class, not enough to become a distraction.

The facility was also very clean and spacious. I got my own locker (that had a combination lock)  and there was a nice changing room. Showers are always key because people who  go to the 5 or 6 am classes (like myself) often go straight to work from there and there is nothing more off putting than having dirty shower stalls or having none at all. Unfortunately, I didn't get a good look at theirs.

There's a special first class rate for new members but otherwise it seriously cost an arm and an leg to go there. These high prices make the studio only accessibly to those who can afford it whereas I think studios should also get gratification from helping people meet their fitness goals.

Overall, try their first class deal and you'll get a great work out but I would rather spend the membership money on supporting a smaller studio/business.</Review>< pics>

<rating>5< /rating>< text>
We enjoyed our one-night stay here (me and my three kids from 7-11). The beds and bedding were very comfy, with more than adequate pillows, and an extra blanket in the bathroom closet. Fun decor throughout, and you can tell they take pride in the place. We ended up in a handicap accessible room, which meant the room was extra small and the bathroom was huge, but it worked out just fine. All the staff we interacted with was very friendly, helpful, and professional. Room was clean and everything worked fine. It was a little noisy at times, but that wasn't an issue for us, since we brought a white noise machine. Zero complaints, but do your homework on where you need to pull in to park. The lobby entrance is kind of in an alley behind the hotel almost. Valet parking is mandatory due to space issues, and there is a nightly fee. (Both of which I was aware of beforehand.)</text>

< Name>
Marianne Borges<//Name>
<Time>1532633268949</Time>< Rate>
4<//Rate>
< review>
If you are a big fan of everything Vintage Hollywood - you'll LOVE this hotel! It's walking distance to Hollywood Blvd and I loved the vintage, art deco feel of the lobby and downstairs area, the 101 Coffee Shop on the main floor is a GREAT place to eat and only adds to the vintage feel! The beds were extremely comfortable and our room was surprisingly roomy! We had three people and lots of bags and still so roomy! Pool and deck,  laundry facilities and vending machines offering candy, pop and laundry detergent was a great plus! Parking was the biggest problem, if you arrive late to the hotel or have a late night....the self park apparently fills up and you're left to the mercy of the valets. Of the three valets we encountered,  two of them were downright rude. Parking was $22 a day for guests, not free and definitely not worth it since the valets treat you like you're a criminal trying to sneak on the property. All the other employees were just wonderful and so friendly!<//review>

<text>What was there NOT to like?? This place was great from the moment we walked in to the time we left. Keith, the desk clerk the night we checked in was a perfect combination of positive energy, professionalism and tourist guide with a fantastic sense of humor. David the other clerk was also extremely nice. We were lucky enough to have gotten a spot in the original building. The pictures that lined the walls gave the perfect atmosphere to being in Hollywood. My favorite was a a nice black and white of Jack Nicholson as the Joker. I'm a sucker for old wooden staircases. The sound they give off when you climb up or down is nostalgic. They say we are old and wary but are still here to welcome you, still strong enough to hold you. We were right on the second floor so I was always happy to climb them. The elevator was the same but a slow elevator seems a little more tired and I hate to have them work. The pool was heated so the kids loved it as they swam under the moonlit night. The color stripe pattern that has been painted on the walls leaves you with a calm. Every guest there was also extremely nice and friendly, and lastly the room itself. Well the room was fantastic. It felt clean and comfortable. They even had a cute little dish there with q tips and cotton balls!!! No one does that anymore. This hotel is close to everything and like a block from highway 101. I will definitely stay here again and will gladly  recommend this hotel to family and friends.</text>< Pics>

<name>Adrian L<//name>< Text>
We stayed at the Best Western as it seemed like a good location in Hollywood for a reasonable price.

Check in was quick and the receptionist gave us a quick run down of nearby things to do and things we could book.

The Elevator is crazily slow, so if you can take the stairs thats recommended.

Note: Twin Queen Room
The room was very large and so was the bathroom. I could best describe the rooms as a good Best Western Style room but if your used to city lux its far from that. The air conditioner unit was a bit louder than I would like but it was not a major issue.

The bathroom could use with a bit of an update but at least the shower was hot.

The beds were comfortable and the TV had a good selection of channels some paid and some free.

The location of this hotel is within a walk to Hollywood blvd and the Hollywood/Vine Metro Station if public transport is the way you are going. The hotel also has a great diner (Cafe 101) which is open late and has some good food.

Overall The Best Western Plus delivered a good stay, it has a lot of memorabilia on the walls which is fascinating and there were no major issues during the stay but I also would not say the hotel is fantastic enough to earn a 5 star stay.</Text>

I loved this place. Our flight was delayed and we arrived at the hotel very late. Check in was a breeze. The room itself was very spacious with a fridge and coffee maker . This is by far the funkiest hotel I have ever stayed in.  The hallways are narrow and the elevator is a really odd shape and only holds three people without luggage.  Parking is a nightmare and poorly signed so you literally have no idea what to do or where to go.  It was clean, the broken A/C unit was replaced while we were out the next day. The bathroom was large and both rooms we had were showers only and the water temperature fluctuated anytime anyone ANYWHERE in the hotel touched anything that had to do with the water system.</Review>

< Text>
Decent hotel with friendly, helpful staff. Nothing fancy but it leaves more money to spend in L.A. (which isn't cheap). It has a small pool, ideal for cooling off and access to a fitness suite, which I didn't see. The attached 101 diner offers typical American fare and is recommended for food at decent prices. The hotel bar, 'Mini Bar' seems to be popular and is a  nice place to relax before going out or on concluding your night. The hotel is only a 10 minute walk from Hollywood Boulevard and another 15 minutes will get you to the main drag at Grauman's Chinese theatre and all the other attractions for tourists. There's a nice bar and eatery area about 10 minutes walk from the hotel along Franklin Avenue.  Seems to be mostly locals using the facilities and that's always a good sign in my book.</Text>

<rating>4<//rating>< text>
A decent hotel very near to the Hollywood walk of fame.

Free parking is available.
During check-in, the visitor has to use the valet parking service only. Later on, he can park the vehicle himself in the designated space.

Passageways have photo frames of well-known Hollywood personalities. That creates an ambience like a film studio.

Rooms are spacious with all the standard amenities.
Wi-Fi is free.
However, morning breakfast is chargeable.

Check-in and checkout were quick. Staff was also polite.<//text>

<UserId.>108920919578840523798</UserId.><Name>Canadi Lynne</Name>< time>
1540181300251<//time>
<Rate>3<//Rate>< Review>
We found this hotel via our travel agent, and it was a mixed bag of experiences. The history of the hotel is fantastic with it's nod to Hollywood decor but once you get passed the amazing autographed photos and elegant lobby you enter into a basic, cramped hotel room.
I will say that the laminate floors were a very nice surprise as was the large double shower in room 119! Unfortunately the very cramped space meant that the bathroom door opened mere inches from the toilet right against the shower. The headboards were orange buttoned upholstry that didn't appear to have been updated for decades! The beds themselves were comfortable though, and the shutters on the windows were great too (I wanted to have them at my house LOL)! Having to open a window (in the shower) onto the pool space to keep humidity out of the bathroom (with or without the shower on) not so great. It lacks privacy and makes for a lot of noise.
We opted not to use the microwave, as there was an actual black burn mark inside on the top of the unit which made us feel unsure of it's safety.
Speaking of safety, if you are not familiar with Hollywood and are traveling as a family, walking this area at dusk or at night isn't exactly comfortable. The area is populated with homeless people (heartbreaking) and those trying to approach you to make a sale. It's an interesting and unique experience but unnerving all the same if you have children with you. Day visits to Hollywood Blvd are better with children.
The man at the front desk with the ginger hair and close kept beard was fantastic! I think he is the manager and I wish I could remember his name to thank him personally. He was always cheerful and helpful with everything! The housekeeping staff was a bit standoffish for some reason, but the valets were always very helpful. I can't complain about the service at all as it was very good.
We didn't get a chance to try the cafe downstairs, but I wish we had. According to the staff, Ryan Gosling comes there for coffee so it must be a pretty great place!
All in all it's a good hotel if you need to be in the area and are simply looking for a place to sleep. Although your sleep may be interrupted if you face the alley like we did as there was arguing and banging at all hours!
A fabulous piece of Hollywood history, but definitely has room for improvement considering the price point!</Review>

<user>104886481928817199242<//user>< Review>
Hotel is older, but refurbishing and updating took place ~5 years ago and was well-planned and very tastefully done. Excellent location and very comfortable room with separate kitchenette area (included bar sink and microwave as well as the usual small refrigerator). The separate bathroom in particular was well-appointed and quite a bit larger than expected(!) with double sinks, plenty of counter space a large, wall-in shower at one end and the clothes closet at the other end. A/C small, but worked fine (and was needed the night we stayed there). TV difficult to figure out and picture kept freezing up every few minutes or so (the only real problem we had). Restaurant food and service was outstanding, although prices were a bit high -- but to be expected given location. (Note: restaurant is affiliated with hotel, but is not owned/operated by Best Western. It's been a popular spot for a very long time for the movie stars who live up in the hills above Franklin/Hollywood Blvd.)</Review>

<UserId.>116244565884251604271</UserId.><text>Service and room was nice. The noise around the hotel was loud.< /text>< name>
Brooks Polowchak</name>
<Rating>4<//Rating><time>1546754781836<//time><GmapID>0x80c2bf3f5c819f95:0xf176859162400874<//GmapID><pics>None<//pics><Response>None<//Response></record></dataset><record>
< review>
The property is well located, however, Hwy 101 is nearby making it a bit noisy. The decor throughout the public spaces is funky retro Hollywood. They have valet parking with in/out privileges, but charge $22/night for your car. The rooms are nice and the beds comfortable. Had the days been slightly warmer we'd have jumped in the beautiful pool! We chose this hotel for its convenient location. From here we could walk into downtown Hollywood, up Beachwood Canyon, to grocery stores (Gelson's and Trader Joe's), the Sunday farmers market, the walk of fame, Grauman's Chinese Theater, etc. With 101 so close it's easy to hop on for trips to Malibu, Ventura, Ojai and other interesting SoCal locales. I'd recommend!</review>

< Review>
I really enjoyed my stay at this hotel. I was there from June 10th to Jun 15th. My flight arrived early and even though check in is at 3, the staff accommodated me and let me check in at 12. The room was clean and the decorations were nice. The staff was very friendly. We weren't too happy with paying for parking each day but its valet and the guys are very friendly. Room service was nice. Anytime we needed more towels or anything they came quickly. If your traveling to LA for leisure and you don't want to spend an arm and a leg on a hotel, this hotel is perfect. I feel it offered a lot and it's really affordable. Its also walking distance from a lot of nice attractions. The only thing I didn't like was the 101 diner. The food was kind of gross. Gave both of us stomach aches. Other than that I highly recommend this hotel but go eat elsewhere. Dolby isn't too far away and they have some good restaurants there.< /Review>

<Text>Our first night here was not so great. Our room was right next to the elevator shaft, so the noise was pretty full on throughout the night. I immediately complained and requested a new room. <Date>1500533777516<//Date><rate>1< /rate><Review>Do not be fooled by this Best Western's marketing ploy of making it seem as though it is a friendly, supportive part of the Hollywood community. I had a friend in town who of course wanted some pictures taken in and around famous Hollywood sites and so of course, being that I live right up the street, we started at the hotel. Management promptly and very rudely ran us off, threatening to call the police on us and have us cited, for literally taking pictures in their side parking lot. No tripod, no lights, no crew, nothing, just a girl from out of town wanting to get some pictures taken at various locations in and around Hollywood. Not blocking foot traffic, street traffic, doorways or walkways, not inhibiting business in any way shape or form. When I explained to the manager what we were doing and that I lived right up the street and frequented his place of business (the front desk attendant recognized me) and that I was not doing a "professional" shoot, he literally got in my face, said "This is Hollywood" and told me that if I didn't leave immediately he would call the cops and have me cited. Do not support this establishment. Take it from a local, there are PLENTY of places of business in the area that are FAR more hospitable for a much better price (and situated in a more convenient local than our friendly manager on the corner). May I suggest the La Belle for month to month parking, it is gated (and their gates WORK), covered, so your car isn't in the weather AND has around the clock security and is quite a bit cheaper than the mid-long term parking at the Best Western. Franklin Village is right down the street and offers infinitely more versatile, sophisticated and price effective dining options. There are countless BEAUTIFUL Air BnBs and hotels in the area that not only offer better prices, but better views as well.
